    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer15591092873968818103">Nooit meer slapen is het meesterlijke verhaal van de jonge geoloog Alfred Issendorf, die in het moerassige noorden van Noorwegen onderzoek wil verrichten om de hypothese van zijn leermeester en promotor Sibbelee te staven. Issendorf is ambitieus: hij hoopt dat hem op deze reis iets groots te wachten staat, dat zijn naam aan een belangrijk wetenschappelijk feit zal worden v</span>
  <span id="freeText15591092873968818103" style="display:none">Nooit meer slapen is het meesterlijke verhaal van de jonge geoloog Alfred Issendorf, die in het moerassige noorden van Noorwegen onderzoek wil verrichten om de hypothese van zijn leermeester en promotor Sibbelee te staven. Issendorf is ambitieus: hij hoopt dat hem op deze reis iets groots te wachten staat, dat zijn naam aan een belangrijk wetenschappelijk feit zal worden verbonden. Deze ambitie hangt samen met het verlangen het werk van zijn vader, die door een ongeluk tijdens een onderzoekstocht om het leven kwam, te voltooien. Nooit meer slapen is een grootse roman over grote dromen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15591092873968818103" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1817988522" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1817988522" />
    <a title="BlackOxford" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17744555-blackoxford"><img alt="BlackOxford" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484863606p2/17744555.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1817988522?book_show_action=true">Nov 22, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BlackOxford" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BlackOxford" href="/user/show/17744555-blackoxford">BlackOxford</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781585675838" href="/book/show/1199067.Beyond_Sleep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17744555-blackoxford?shelf=dutch-flemish">dutch-flemish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1817988522" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14915168951579908215"><b>Gezellig om thuis te blijven</b><br/><br/>Beyond Sleep is a novel of the Dutchman Abroad, a genre not without charm but perhaps an acquired taste. Its moral is typical of the genre: Gezellig om thuis te blijven, It's probably best not to leave the front garden. It was written in 1966 but remained untranslated into English for forty years. This delay makes it even more of a period piece, expressing some of the most important self-criticisms of Dutch society of the time at an effective and safe distance. <br/><br/>Beyond</span>
  <span id="freeText14915168951579908215" style="display:none"><b>Gezellig om thuis te blijven</b><br /><br />Beyond Sleep is a novel of the Dutchman Abroad, a genre not without charm but perhaps an acquired taste. Its moral is typical of the genre: Gezellig om thuis te blijven, It's probably best not to leave the front garden. It was written in 1966 but remained untranslated into English for forty years. This delay makes it even more of a period piece, expressing some of the most important self-criticisms of Dutch society of the time at an effective and safe distance. <br /><br />Beyond Sleep was written at an important juncture in Dutch history - less than a generation after collaboration with the Nazis as well as the brutal suppression of the Indonesian independence movement; and during a period of growing unrest about immigration from another soon-to-be former colony, the South American country of Suriname. National guilt and a residual Calvinistic moral sensitivity had reached a high point. Simultaneously a growing nationalism and racism were threatening the live-and-let-live equilibrium of a traditionally highly diverse society. What better literary way to relieve some of the tension while addressing the situation than to place a story in an even smaller country than The Netherlands, namely Norway at a third its population, and to play Dutch conditions against a nationalism and racism of the East Norwegians with regard to the West Norwegians (a standard Dutch joke) as well as the Lapps of the North? The implication is clear: Holland is not at all a bad place to be despite contemporary problems.<br /><br />Unfortunately, the running in-jokes about Dutch provincialism, practical ineptitude, and lack of worldly wisdom are unlikely to be recognised as such by those unfamiliar with Dutch culture. They are probably too dated even for the Dutch, especially the younger generations. Not that Hermans isn't a competent writer, he is first rate, as is Ina Rilke's translation. Nevertheless, unless the alternating dry and slapstick wit of The Netherlands of mid-twentieth century are your nieuwe haring, you may not want to invest the time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14915168951579908215" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_384393546" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/384393546" />
    <a title="Marc" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2876105-marc"><img alt="Marc" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569160429p2/2876105.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/384393546?book_show_action=true">Aug 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Marc" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Marc" href="/user/show/2876105-marc">Marc</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2876105-marc?shelf=dutch-literature">dutch-literature</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer384393546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7793664244676233560">The most neat Dutch novel I have ever read: a cunningly balanced composition (contrary to the other work of Hermans), beautifully written (especially the desolate 'jungle' of Lapland), and with a clear focus on the absurdity of life, religion and even science. The notorious gloominess of Hermans is all around, especially in the 'philosopical' conversations of Alfred with other hikers and with himself, but it isn't vexatious, on the contrary, it seems very natural. Beautiful.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_925198" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/925198" />
    <a title="elisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66278-elisa"><img alt="elisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1227614791p2/66278.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer13756646287291752803">how strange that this book has made such an impression on me; the topic is not among my interests, there is not much going on and the protagonist is a bit of an insecure, self-centred idiot - still the descriptions of the norwegian landscape, the highly philosophical conversations between the characters and in general hermans' style create a strangely gripping if desolate atmosphere. </span>

<div id="review_63943290" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63943290" />
    <a title="Stephen Durrant" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1457001-stephen-durrant"><img alt="Stephen Durrant" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1362701086p2/1457001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63943290?book_show_action=true">Jul 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephen Durrant" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephen Durrant" href="/user/show/1457001-stephen-durrant">Stephen Durrant</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781585679881" href="/book/show/3078287-beyond-sleep">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63943290" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8151424975091577131">W.F. Hermans (1921-1995) is one of the most highly acclaimed post-war Dutch writers. The first two-thirds or so of this novel is Kafkaesque. A somewhat hapless young scientist, eager to prove that small circles of water in northern Norway were caused by meteors, joins up with three more hardened and extremely strange scientists on a geological expedition. He is hardly up to the task and stumbles from one mishap to another, all absurd and at times quite funny. But Hermans seems to have a more ser</span>
  <span id="freeText8151424975091577131" style="display:none">W.F. Hermans (1921-1995) is one of the most highly acclaimed post-war Dutch writers. The first two-thirds or so of this novel is Kafkaesque. A somewhat hapless young scientist, eager to prove that small circles of water in northern Norway were caused by meteors, joins up with three more hardened and extremely strange scientists on a geological expedition. He is hardly up to the task and stumbles from one mishap to another, all absurd and at times quite funny. But Hermans seems to have a more serious message in mind. Our hero, who believes his significance as a human being can only be affirmed through a stunning scientific discovery, soon begins to learn about himself and his capacities of endurance. He eventually comes to realize that what he is striving for will not win him scientific immortality: "I am building a cathedral of unknown proportions, and by the time it is finished I will be long dead and no-one will ever know of my contribution" (p. 119). Perhaps the most noteworthy parts of "Beyond Sleep," at least to this reader, are the philosophical/scientific observations and nice, brief comments about the nature of existence that dot the text. A somewhat humorous example of the former is the following (keep in mind that mosquitoes play a prominent role in this novel . . . like so often in literature set in Scandinavia): "I often wonder whether people realise that they might be completely mistaken about their place in the scheme of things. Remember that stuff about the first being last, the last first? Who's to say we won't be welcomed into the afterlife by a host of mosquitoes? Wielding the sceptre up on the big throne could be a virus--the foot-and-mouth virus, say" (p. 149). As an example of a comment on the absurd nature of our existence, here's a nice statement about how man can keep his self-respect: "By doing his duty, the incomprehensible duty imposed on him by his incomprehensible existence in an incomprehensible world" (p. 176). Yes on that . . . and yes on much else in this book. But two hundred pages of tramping through mosquito-infested sub-artic Norway was a bit much . . . perhaps it was reminiscent of too many unpleasant moments I experienced growing up in Alaska!</span>
  <a data-text-id="8151424975091577131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1198724773?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Laura" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Laura" href="/user/show/21105534-laura">Laura</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789023435648" href="/book/show/6659993-nooit-meer-slapen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21105534-laura?shelf=classic">classic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1198724773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14981259332369902283">To be honest I'm not a big fan of dutch literature, but I actually enjoyed this book. Although the story started of slow, it slowly started to develop until I was really intrigued by the story line. <br/><br/>What made the book special in my opinion was the fact that everything you could think of was written down. For example, when Alfred is walking 25 kilometers and starts to get tired, he counts his steps and is encouraging himself to continue his journey. Every normal person does this (at least I think</span>
  <span id="freeText14981259332369902283" style="display:none">To be honest I'm not a big fan of dutch literature, but I actually enjoyed this book. Although the story started of slow, it slowly started to develop until I was really intrigued by the story line. <br /><br />What made the book special in my opinion was the fact that everything you could think of was written down. For example, when Alfred is walking 25 kilometers and starts to get tired, he counts his steps and is encouraging himself to continue his journey. Every normal person does this (at least I think so) but to see it actually written down on paper shocked me a little. Alfred's thoughts fly everywhere and I think Hermans did a great job by writing down all of them.<br /><br />The plot itself was evenly surprising, I didn't expect a lot of things to happen and normally plots don't really surprise me because most of the time they are very predictable. <br /><br />I rated the book 4 stars and not 5 because of the slow beginning, but if you're searching for some refreshing literature you should definitely read this!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2960147904" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2960147904" />
    <a title="Evi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41190345-evi"><img alt="Evi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601748069p2/41190345.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2960147904?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evi" href="/user/show/41190345-evi">Evi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9789023455837" href="/book/show/13543973-nooit-meer-slapen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41190345-evi?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41190345-evi?shelf=dutch">dutch</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41190345-evi?shelf=1950-1974">1950-1974</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41190345-evi?shelf=travel">travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41190345-evi?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41190345-evi?shelf=top-10-beste-nederlandse-boeken-ooi">top-10-beste-nederlandse-boeken-ooi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2960147904" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5422259120577580958">Oh wow, this was really really boring.<br/><br/>I was kind of ashamed that I hadn't read a Dutch book this year, but also in general, I read very little books that are published in the Netherlands. So I found a list made by a big Dutch newspaper with the 10 best Dutch books ever. I had only read one book on that list and that was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1877062.Het_huis_van_de_moskee' title='Het huis van de moskee by Kader Abdolah' rel='nofollow noopener'>Het huis van de moskee</a> and I really liked that one plus the list contained some other well known books that you "have to read", so I thought; let's try to read the books on this </span>
  <span id="freeText5422259120577580958" style="display:none">Oh wow, this was really really boring.<br /><br />I was kind of ashamed that I hadn't read a Dutch book this year, but also in general, I read very little books that are published in the Netherlands. So I found a list made by a big Dutch newspaper with the 10 best Dutch books ever. I had only read one book on that list and that was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1877062.Het_huis_van_de_moskee" title="Het huis van de moskee by Kader Abdolah" rel="nofollow noopener">Het huis van de moskee</a> and I really liked that one plus the list contained some other well known books that you "have to read", so I thought; let's try to read the books on this list. <br /><br />Unfortunately I really can not not finish a book, especially when it's on a list like that, which means that apparently a lot of people think it is really good. But I just really really don't see why. Everything was so slow and nothing really happened and it made me fall a sleep every night after a few pages. So halfway I decided to switch to the audio book, in the hope that that would make it a little less boring. But even the audio book was very monotonous and my mind kept wandering off. And it's not that it's badly written, but it's also not spectacular. <br /><br />So when I was at about 70% of the book I started googling why you should read this book. Unfortunately that also resulted in me finding out the big thing that happens in the end of the book, so even the most exciting thing that happens in this book was ruined for me. And I still haven't found out why people think this is good..<br /><br />So not a great pick to start to read more (classic) Dutch books. <br /><br /><b>2 stars</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="5422259120577580958" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

It's extremely well-written; a truly great command of language.<br/><br/>I’d read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12792022.De_donkere_kamer_van_Damokles' title='De donkere kamer van Damokles by Willem Frederik Hermans' rel='nofollow noopener'>De donkere kamer van Damokles</a> (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2312935.The_Darkroom_of_Damocles' title='The Darkroom of Damocles by Willem Frederik Hermans' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Darkroom of Damocles</a>), the book <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/184683.Willem_Frederik_Hermans' title='Willem Frederik Hermans' rel='nofollow noopener'>Willem Frederik Hermans</a> is probably most famous for, a couple of years ago but <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13543973.Nooit_meer_slapen' title='Nooit meer slapen by Willem Frederik Hermans' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nooit meer slapen</a> (<a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1199067.Beyond_Sleep' title='Beyond Sleep by Willem Frederik Hermans' rel='nofollow noopener'>Beyond Sleep</a>), published some eight years later, is far better in my opinion.<br/><br/><i>Nooit meer slapen</i> tells the story of Alfred Is</span>
  <span id="freeText2650565134432017628" style="display:none">Gelezen voor <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18141925-current-group-read-30-nooit-meer-slapen-by-willem-frederik-hermans" rel="nofollow noopener">Group Read #30</a> van de Netherlands &amp; Flanders group. Zie onder ander <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18141925-current-group-read-30-nooit-meer-slapen-by-willem-frederik-hermans#comment_154138252" rel="nofollow noopener">bericht #17 aldaar.</a><br /><br /><br />What an incredibly good book this is... It's extremely well-written; a truly great command of language.<br /><br />I’d read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12792022.De_donkere_kamer_van_Damokles" title="De donkere kamer van Damokles by Willem Frederik Hermans" rel="nofollow noopener">De donkere kamer van Damokles</a> (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2312935.The_Darkroom_of_Damocles" title="The Darkroom of Damocles by Willem Frederik Hermans" rel="nofollow noopener">The Darkroom of Damocles</a>), the book <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/184683.Willem_Frederik_Hermans" title="Willem Frederik Hermans" rel="nofollow noopener">Willem Frederik Hermans</a> is probably most famous for, a couple of years ago but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13543973.Nooit_meer_slapen" title="Nooit meer slapen by Willem Frederik Hermans" rel="nofollow noopener">Nooit meer slapen</a> (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1199067.Beyond_Sleep" title="Beyond Sleep by Willem Frederik Hermans" rel="nofollow noopener">Beyond Sleep</a>), published some eight years later, is far better in my opinion.<br /><br /><i>Nooit meer slapen</i> tells the story of Alfred Issendorf, a 25-year-old geologist who is going to the northern part of Norway, the land where the sun never sets during summer, to do research into the possible presence of meteorites and their craters. The results of this research he intends to use in obtaining his doctorate. He will be joining three Norwegian researchers while going to the inhabitable north.<br /><br />Alfred's preparations for the actual expedition are not quite what one would expect, which made me wonder where the story would lead to. Although the book is not thrilling or sensational in the ordinary sense, it managed to keep me spellbound till the very last page. A truly marvellous story...</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2601396318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11039752324681333844">Willem Frederik Hermans is yet another excellent foreign writer it has taken anglo-sphere publishers too long to translate. <br/>Written over half a century ago, Beyond Sleep is set in a world before GPS and widespread communications, when it was all too easy to get lost. Hermans’ depiction of the sheer physicality of tramping across arctic tundra, under relentless attack from mosquitoes and flies, with a heavy pack, inappropriate footwear and faulty equipment is harrowing. The constant daylight erod</span>
  <span id="freeText11039752324681333844" style="display:none">Willem Frederik Hermans is yet another excellent foreign writer it has taken anglo-sphere publishers too long to translate. <br />Written over half a century ago, Beyond Sleep is set in a world before GPS and widespread communications, when it was all too easy to get lost. Hermans’ depiction of the sheer physicality of tramping across arctic tundra, under relentless attack from mosquitoes and flies, with a heavy pack, inappropriate footwear and faulty equipment is harrowing. The constant daylight erodes the protagonist’s sense of time, reinforcing his sense of being lost in a place where even the geology is questionable. But sometimes we must take a wrong turn in order to discover our true direction. <br />Despite being about losing one’s way, of losing one’s footing, Hermans’ narrative progresses with an even, sure pace; and very tidily concludes with a real cosmic bang. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11039752324681333844" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_22621991" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/22621991" />
    <a title="P." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/236606-p"><img alt="P." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464748215p2/236606.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/22621991?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="P." class="user" itemprop="url" name="P." href="/user/show/236606-p">P.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781585675838" href="/book/show/1199067.Beyond_Sleep">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/236606-p?shelf=fictive">fictive</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer22621991" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10774496612915793546">Having put this on my to-read list in 2007, I wasn't quite sure what this book would be about or why I thought I'd like it. Luckily, I know myself well and/or the review that I read was spot on. <br/><br/>The story of our geologist Alfred's journey in Finnmark is slowly paced. Alfred has a horrible time but ends up with a kind of Stockholm Syndrome for the desolate landscape, constant wetness and attack by mosquitoes and fies, and ill-preparedness of the whole thing. It's a wilderness trial, and that he c</span>
  <span id="freeText10774496612915793546" style="display:none">Having put this on my to-read list in 2007, I wasn't quite sure what this book would be about or why I thought I'd like it. Luckily, I know myself well and/or the review that I read was spot on. <br /><br />The story of our geologist Alfred's journey in Finnmark is slowly paced. Alfred has a horrible time but ends up with a kind of Stockholm Syndrome for the desolate landscape, constant wetness and attack by mosquitoes and fies, and ill-preparedness of the whole thing. It's a wilderness trial, and that he can just survive it becomes the most important thing to Alfred. For he's a mixture of grand ambition and existential despair, mixed with increasing paranoid frettings re: his place in the world and with his expedition companions. I was able to feel a happy-terrible identification with him while also thinking that I'd react much more sensibly. A fun reading space, really.<br /><br />I would have loved to see this book adapted by Michelangelo Antonioni. <br /><br />I can't leave the review without giving some examples of Alfred's voice:<br /><br />"I feel an irresistible urge to conjure up the worst possible scenario: that all my efforts will have been wasted. Think of those occasional boulders you see on the moors in eastern Holland--who's to say they weren't dragged there by some primitive man, slaving away year in year out to advance half a metre a day, sleeping beside his boulder at night...<br /><br />"No horses in those days. Let's hope primitive man was aware of the possibility of using tree trunks as levers. He grew old. People aged much more rapidly in those days. My barrow-builder, grizzled by the age of thirty! Fell ill and had to give up long before his boulder was close enough to another one for us, his descendants, to think: Hey! A barrow for the dead!" (p. 140)<br /><br />Unknown barrow-builders are something of a theme for Alfred...<br />Here's an example of his doomed research with a plum simile at the end:<br /><br />"I explored eight small round lakes today. Walked around each one, inspecting the margins for any ridges or ramparts. Most meteor craters are encircled by a low bank of matter thrown up by the stone's impact. Didn't see anything noteworthy. Slowing down to a snail's pace, I became increasingly aware of the raindrops impacting on the water, making it squirt up thickly like ripe tomato juice." (p. 180)<br /><br />And finally a great example of peevishness:<br /><br />"I will get the hang of climbing rocks and crossing rivers eventually, I suppose, but not of drawing. I tried hard since early childhood, but it never amounted to anything. I could never stand all those psychologists theorising about the naive creative urge in the very young, claiming that kids draw cars with square wheels because they live <i>in a world of their own!</i><br /><br />"The world I live in has never been a world of my own, it existed long before I came into it and I do not recall ever thinking cars had square wheels, not even when I was five and drawing them like that." (p. 225)<br /><br />Here's to hoping there are more Hermans books in translation.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10774496612915793546" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_892308106" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/892308106" />
    <a title="BellaGBear" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14546476-bellagbear"><img alt="BellaGBear" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1390168030p2/14546476.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/892308106?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="BellaGBear" class="user" itemprop="url" name="BellaGBear" href="/user/show/14546476-bellagbear">BellaGBear</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14546476-bellagbear?shelf=bookworms-united">bookworms-united</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14546476-bellagbear?shelf=owned-books">owned-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14546476-bellagbear?shelf=dutch">dutch</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer892308106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10845318150164934397">This book has left quite an impression on me. Not immediately upon finishing though, but the book kept popping into my mind days after I’d finished it as if the book had wormed its way into my mind. That could be because the plot of a guy going abroad to do research to make a name for himself in science resonated with me because I am also going abroad to do research in a few weeks. But maybe it was the oppressive underlying atmosphere of dread and futility that kept me reading. It reads a bit as</span>
  <span id="freeText10845318150164934397" style="display:none">This book has left quite an impression on me. Not immediately upon finishing though, but the book kept popping into my mind days after I’d finished it as if the book had wormed its way into my mind. That could be because the plot of a guy going abroad to do research to make a name for himself in science resonated with me because I am also going abroad to do research in a few weeks. But maybe it was the oppressive underlying atmosphere of dread and futility that kept me reading. It reads a bit as a train wreck: you know something bad is going to happen, but you can’t look away.<br /><br />This book shows in a brilliant way how futile life can be and how even the greatest efforts can lead to absolutely nothing. The main person in this book, Alfred, is a young geologist working on his PhD. He goes to Finnmark, in the utmost north of Norway, to study rocks and the landscape. By doing that he hopes to find proof for the proposition of his Professor Sibbelee that there are meteorite craters in the area.<br /><br />(...)<br /><br />This is the kind of book in which not much happens but in a good way. Most of the text are descriptions of Alfred’s doubts, of camping or of walking through a landscape difficult to navigate with fifteen kilos on your back. From the start, you, as a reader, wonder how he is going to manage his research, and when he arrives at the research destination, very little is talked about his research, while there is mentioning of the studies of the other three persons. It seems that not having the aerial photographs has shaken Alfred to such an extent that he doesn’t know what to do next. He starts doubting the proposition as well, which was never his own idea. That might be exactly why he failed. Throughout the book, events lead him instead of the other way around. Even his choice to become a geologist was prompted by his dead father because he died leaving his scientific promise unfulfilled. In the field, it becomes clear he is ill-prepared for his fieldwork and he even questions what he is doing in Norway as a Dutch guy. He wonders what he can possibly discover that the Norwegians haven’t found themselves already. Especially when details are revealed about why he did not get the aerial photographs from Numendal. There is no kindness in the book for the characters, and they certainly don’t have it for each other. Alfred moves in a dog-eat-dog world where his youth and naivety is used to fight out old battles between professors and in which there is no room for an insecure naive boy to make a name for himself.<br /><br />(...)<br /><br /><i> Read the full review at <a href="https://bookwormsshallruletheworld.wordpress.com/2018/07/24/beyond-sleep-nooit-meer-slapen-willem-frederik-hermans/" rel="nofollow noopener">Bookworms United</a> </i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10845318150164934397" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1306662633?book_show_action=true">Jun 13, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Einu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Einu" href="/user/show/2499920-einu">Einu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9789023492528" href="/book/show/24383134-nooit-meer-slapen">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2499920-einu?shelf=thought-provoking-fiction">thought-provoking-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1306662633" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15292884468762216090">Alfred is ambitious. He wants to do something exceptional. He doesn’t just want to get a PhD, he wants to get it by finding something truly remarkable. His ambition comes with a certain degree of arrogance. He looks down on a lot of people, like the near-blind (and in his mind self-indulgent) geology professor who “wastes” Alfred’s time by giving him unsolicited lectures. This arrogance seems to be a shield, meant to protect him from a deeprooted sense of insecurity. He distrusts people, assumin</span>
  <span id="freeText15292884468762216090" style="display:none">Alfred is ambitious. He wants to do something exceptional. He doesn’t just want to get a PhD, he wants to get it by finding something truly remarkable. His ambition comes with a certain degree of arrogance. He looks down on a lot of people, like the near-blind (and in his mind self-indulgent) geology professor who “wastes” Alfred’s time by giving him unsolicited lectures. This arrogance seems to be a shield, meant to protect him from a deeprooted sense of insecurity. He distrusts people, assuming they judge him just like he judges them. By looking down on them, their opinions can’t truly hurt. His insecurity goes hand in hand with a feeling of incompetence. Once he has embarked on his expedition to the north of Norway, he realises more and more how unprepared he is to perform his research; thinking to himself that he has the wit to achieve good academic results but not the essence to be a truly good geologist, always forgetting to pay attention to what is actually of importance.<br /><br />One scene that illustrates this beautifuly is when he thinks back to a field trip in the north of Sweden, when the group comes upon a forty-metre-deep lake, which is said to be so clear that you can see the bottom when you swim in it. Only Alfred and one other student dare to take a leap into the ice-cold lake, but once they are back on the shore and the other student asks him whether he could see the ground, Alfred realises that he forgot to look down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15292884468762216090" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Irony at the end: possible account of what he has been looking all along and does not see when it appears (meteorite). Death of companion and entries in his journal turns narrator's version into absurd caricature of what happened. (Passage in Tromso)</span>

<div id="review_939267598" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/939267598" />
    <a title="Anders Choy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18524861-anders-choy"><img alt="Anders Choy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363718992p2/18524861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anders Choy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anders Choy" href="/user/show/18524861-anders-choy">Anders Choy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer939267598" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15933218296503450790">"Beyond Sleep" is an existentialist book strongly influenced by a masculine Kafkaesque tone, but then spiced up with some low key deadpan dry humour.<br/>It essentially revolves around an average scientist who wants to make it big - partly to make his father proud - only to find out, in the face of the pure and tough nature of Norwegian Finnmark, that he is just that, average - or at least, just human. A wonderful conclusion and a wonderful journey to witness.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<span id="freeTextContainer7859477653766887522">Hermans surely knows how to write. I love his prose, the way he evokes the landscape above the polar circle. I don't do well with narrow perspective, depressed characters point-of-views, so I put the book aside. </span>

<div id="review_2987980612" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2987980612" />
    <a title="Michael Haase" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36432305-michael-haase"><img alt="Michael Haase" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1498749694p2/36432305.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2987980612?book_show_action=true">Sep 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Michael Haase" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Michael Haase" href="/user/show/36432305-michael-haase">Michael Haase</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781585675838" href="/book/show/1199067.Beyond_Sleep">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2987980612" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17772370114439354180">A book about a man falling short of his expectations. How fitting then that this book should fall so short of mine. I had great patience with this book. I trekked across 178 pages of it, at least a whole 2/3rds of the thing, but sadly I found the plot is just as empty as the book's landscape. <br/><br/>The story progresses at an UNBEARABLY slow pace, with the narrator's journey (the main focus of the book) not even beginning until about 50 pages in. And even then a lot of the text is just given to the nar</span>
  <span id="freeText17772370114439354180" style="display:none">A book about a man falling short of his expectations. How fitting then that this book should fall so short of mine. I had great patience with this book. I trekked across 178 pages of it, at least a whole 2/3rds of the thing, but sadly I found the plot is just as empty as the book's landscape. <br /><br />The story progresses at an UNBEARABLY slow pace, with the narrator's journey (the main focus of the book) not even beginning until about 50 pages in. And even then a lot of the text is just given to the narrator's whiny drivel about mosquitoes and other little things. 178 pages in and the most significant thing to happen on the journey is the protagonist gets his leg wet. <br /><br />The protagonist, Issendorf, is not very compelling. He's very whiny, self-absorbed, and pessimistic. He has a mother that is a scumbag. <br /><br />Bizarrely enough, the book is also full of random facts that are most likely false such as: the founders of major religions have mostly been fishermen, Columbus discovered America in a row boat, the Aztecs made human sacrifices every day like an alarm clock going off each morning, Dolmen builders dragged capstones into place by hand over a period of hundreds of years, and many more. <br /><br />The writing style is nothing spectacular. A heck of a lot about arial photos and mosquitoes, my god!<br /><br />Overall, the book wouldn't be so bad if it was much shorter. To quote the author, <i>"How many writers wrote a thousand pages about something that they could have told about in just a hundred pages?"</i><br /><br />Many people refer to this novel as a Dutch classic. I think this book proves that just about anything could be called a "classic".</span>
  <a data-text-id="17772370114439354180" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2120002514" />
    <a title="Lisanne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15053417-lisanne"><img alt="Lisanne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1358932259p2/15053417.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2120002514?book_show_action=true">Sep 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisanne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisanne" href="/user/show/15053417-lisanne">Lisanne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2120002514" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4428158875600315588">Reading this at 25 while feeling a bit anxious about your first big solo trip and actually going to Norway was maybe not the best time to read it... <br/><br/>Or actually, maybe it was. While my trains and busses were not doing what they were supposed to be doing, Alfred's leg was torn apart so everytime I felt a bit helpless, I thought "well, at least I'm better off than those guys". Finishing this at Sørenga, overlooking the Oslofjord, was pretty great, I'd have to say. <br/><br/>Apart from that, I thoroughly enj</span>
  <span id="freeText4428158875600315588" style="display:none">Reading this at 25 while feeling a bit anxious about your first big solo trip and actually going to Norway was maybe not the best time to read it... <br /><br />Or actually, maybe it was. While my trains and busses were not doing what they were supposed to be doing, Alfred's leg was torn apart so everytime I felt a bit helpless, I thought "well, at least I'm better off than those guys". Finishing this at Sørenga, overlooking the Oslofjord, was pretty great, I'd have to say. <br /><br />Apart from that, I thoroughly enjoyed the story and the writing. I have always put off reading Hermans because my most-hated Dutch teacher was his biggest fan, but I have to give it to him now: he's a great writer.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4428158875600315588" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('HVlMIhHCDXxNoWtQEqZdFVy43c1y+XtbXwXIieqk1sdAIatmtMwFbL+4A/0xntn6vgMy0jIB0eA/gSZFIIFT5g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('CfJjaFbsChJ8j6arddkQmLZdsv/qQNMoi/B5CXyIYFFUioQs8+ICAo6WzgZW4ZR3VOZd4Kq4eZPrdJfFtq3lcA==')})
  }
//]]>

          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/184683.Willem_Frederik_Hermans">About Willem Frederik Hermans</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/184683.Willem_Frederik_Hermans"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1251877831p3/184683.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/184683.Willem_Frederik_Hermans">Willem Frederik Hermans
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
222
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8594725105242805472">Willem Frederik Hermans is one of the greatest post-war Dutch authors. Before devoting his entire life to writing, Hermans had been teaching Physical Geography at the University of Groningen for many years. He had already started writing and publishing in magazines at a young age. His polemic and provocative style led to a court case as early as 1952. His caustic pieces were compiled in Mandarijne</span>
  <span id="freeText8594725105242805472" style="display:none">Willem Frederik Hermans is one of the greatest post-war Dutch authors. Before devoting his entire life to writing, Hermans had been teaching Physical Geography at the University of Groningen for many years. He had already started writing and publishing in magazines at a young age. His polemic and provocative style led to a court case as early as 1952. His caustic pieces were compiled in Mandarijnen op zwavelzuur (Mandarines in Sulphuric Acid, 1963), which was reprinted with additions a number of times. It is Hermans’s belief that in order to survive people have to create their own reality. It is inevitable that all these experiences of reality will collide. Language is essential to create order out of chaos and plays an important role in this process. In his essays on Wittgenstein, Hermans studied this problem in depth. In his novels and stories Hermans places his characters in a world of certainty for themselves but equivocal for the reader. It is in this field of tension that the intrigue in De tranen der acacia’s (Acacia’s Tears, 1949) and in De donkere kamer van Damocles (The Darkroom of Damocles, 1958) develops. Although stories such as Moedwil en misverstand (Malice and Misunderstanding) and Paranoia have a surrealistic tendency, Hermans’ novels The Darkroom Of Damocles, Nooit meer slapen (Beyond Sleep), Uit talloos veel miljoenen (From Countless Millions) are more realistic or satirical and everything in his rich oeuvre is subordinate to the author’s pessimistic philosophy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8594725105242805472" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
